2x" data-file-width="462" data-file-height="438" /></a></div>\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Aberfan disaster</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"><div id="mw-fr-revisiontag" class="flaggedrevs_short flaggedrevs_stable_synced plainlinks noprint nomobile"><div class="flaggedrevs_short_basic"><img class="flaggedrevs-icon" src="/w/extensions/FlaggedRevs/frontend/modules/img/doc-magnify.png" 2018</i>.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Catastrophic collapse of colliery spoil tip in Wales </div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n\n\n</p>\n<table class="infobox vevent" style="width:22em"><caption class="summary">Aberfan disaster</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-bottom:#aaa solid 1px">\n<a href="/wiki/File:Aberfan_disaster,_October_1966.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Aberfan disaster, October 1966.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b3/Aberfan_disaster%2C_October_1966.jpg/240px-Aberfan_disaster%2C_October_1966.jpg" width="240" height="330" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/b3/Aberfan_disaster%2C_October_1966.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="269" data-file-height="370" /></a><div>Aberfan in the days immediately after the disaster, showing the extent of the spoil slip</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Date</th><td style="text-align: left;">\n21&#160;October&#160;1966<span style="display:none">&#160;(<span class="bday dtstart published updated">1966-10-21</span>)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Location</th><td class="location" style="text-align: left;">\n<a href="/wiki/Aberfan" title="Aberfan">Aberfan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glamorgan" title="Glamorgan">Glamorgan</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Wales" title="South Wales">South Wales</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Coordinates</a></th><td style="text-align: left;">\n<span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Aberfan_disaster&amp;params=51_41_41_N_3_20_51_W_region:GB_type:event"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">51\xc2\xb041\xe2\x80\xb241\xe2\x80\xb3N</span> <span class="longitude">3\xc2\xb020\xe2\x80\xb251\xe2\x80\xb3W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">51.69472\xc2\xb0N 3.34750\xc2\xb0W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">51.69472; -3.34750</span></span></span></a></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Deaths</th><td style="text-align: left;">\n144 (28 adults, 116 children)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Inquiries</th><td style="text-align: left;">\n<a href="/wiki/Aberfan_Disaster_Tribunal" title="Aberfan Disaster Tribunal">Aberfan Disaster Tribunal</a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-top: #aaa 1px solid;">\nResulted in the passing of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Acts_of_the_Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom,_1960-1979" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Acts of the Parliament of the United Kingdom, 1960-1979">Mines and Quarries (Tips) Act 1969</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Aberfan disaster</b> was the catastrophic collapse of a <a href="/wiki/Colliery" class="mw-redirect" title="Colliery">colliery</a> <a href="/wiki/Spoil_tip" title="Spoil tip">spoil tip</a> at around 9:15&#160;am on 21 October 1966. The tip had been created on a mountain slope above the Welsh village of <a href="/wiki/Aberfan" title="Aberfan">Aberfan</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Merthyr_Tydfil" title="Merthyr Tydfil">Merthyr Tydfil</a> and overlaid a natural spring. A period of heavy rain led to a build-up of water within the tip which caused it to suddenly slide downhill as a <a href="/wiki/Slurry" title="Slurry">slurry</a>, killing 116 children and 28 adults as it engulfed the local <a href="/wiki/Junior_school" title="Junior school">junior school</a> and other buildings. The tip was the responsibility of the <a href="/wiki/National_Coal_Board" title="National Coal Board">National Coal Board</a> (NCB), and the <a href="/wiki/Aberfan_Disaster_Tribunal" title="Aberfan Disaster Tribunal">subsequent inquiry</a> placed the blame for the disaster on the organisation and nine named employees.\n</p><p>There were seven spoil tips on the slopes above Aberfan; Tip 7\xe2\x80\x94the one that slipped onto the village\xe2\x80\x94was begun in 1958 and, at the time of the disaster, was 111 feet (34&#160;m) high. In contravention of the NCB\'s official procedures, the tip was partly based on ground from which water springs emerged. After three weeks of heavy rain the tip was saturated and approximately 140,000 cubic yards (110,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of spoil slipped down the side of the hill and onto the Pantglas area of the village. The main building hit was Pantglas Junior School, where lessons had just begun; 5 teachers and 109 children were killed in the school.\n</p><p>An official inquiry was chaired by <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Appeal_judge_(England_and_Wales)" title="Court of Appeal judge (England and Wales)">Lord Justice</a> <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Davies,_Baron_Edmund-Davies" title="Edmund Davies, Baron Edmund-Davies">Edmund Davies</a>. The report placed the blame squarely on the NCB. The organisation\'s chairman, <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Robens,_Baron_Robens_of_Woldingham" title="Alfred Robens, Baron Robens of Woldingham">Lord Robens</a>, was criticised for making misleading statements and for not providing clarity as to the NCB\'s knowledge of the presence of water springs on the hillside. Neither the NCB nor any of its employees were prosecuted and the organisation was not fined.\n</p><p>The Aberfan Disaster Memorial Fund (ADMF) was set up on the day of the disaster. It received nearly 88,000 contributions, totalling \xc2\xa31.75&#160;million. The remaining tips were removed only after a lengthy fight by Aberfan residents, against resistance from the NCB and the government on the grounds of cost. Clearing was paid for by a government grant and a forced contribution of \xc2\xa3150,000 taken from the memorial fund. In 1997 the British government paid back the \xc2\xa3150,000 to the ADMF, and in 2007 the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="Welsh Assembly">Welsh Assembly</a> donated \xc2\xa31.5 million to the fund and \xc2\xa3500,000 to the Aberfan Education Charity as recompense for the money wrongly taken. Many of the village\'s residents suffered medical problems, and half the survivors have experienced <a href="/wiki/Post-traumatic_stress_disorder" class="mw-redirect" title="Post-traumatic stress disorder">post-traumatic stress disorder</a> at some time in their lives.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aberfan_disaster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="noviewer thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px"><div style="position:relative;width:170px;border:1px solid lightgray"><a href="/wiki/File:Merthyr_Tydfil_UK_location_map.svg" class="image" title="Aberfan is located in Merthyr Tydfil"><img alt="Aberfan is located in Merthyr Tydfil" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Merthyr_Tydfil_UK_location_map.svg/170px-Merthyr_Tydfil_UK_location_map.svg.png" width="170" height="228" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Merthyr_Tydfil_UK_location_map.svg/255px-Merthyr_Tydfil_UK_location_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Merthyr_Tydfil_UK_location_map.svg/340px-Merthyr_Tydfil_UK_location_map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="942" data-file-height="1266" /></a><div style="position:absolute;top:74.627%;left:61.711%"><div style="position:absolute;left:-4px;top:-4px;line-height:0"><img alt="Aberfan" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/8px-Red_pog.svg.png" title="Aberfan" width="8" height="8" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/12px-Red_pog.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/16px-Red_pog.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="64" data-file-height="64" /></div><div style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:-0.75em;left:5px;text-align:left"><div style="display:inline;padding:1px;float:left">Aberfan</div></div></div></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Merthyr_Tydfil_UK_location_map.svg" title="File:Merthyr Tydfil UK location map.svg"> </a></div>Aberfan, Mid Glamorgan</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Aberfan" title="Aberfan">Aberfan</a> is situated toward the bottom of the western valley slope of the Taff Valley, on the eastern slope of <a href="/wiki/Mynydd_Merthyr" title="Mynydd Merthyr">Mynydd Merthyr</a> hill, approximately four miles (6&#160;km) south of <a href="/wiki/Merthyr_Tydfil" title="Merthyr Tydfil">Merthyr Tydfil</a>. When the <a href="/wiki/Merthyr_Vale" title="Merthyr Vale">Merthyr Vale</a> Colliery was sunk on 23 August 1869 by <a href="/wiki/John_Nixon_(mining_engineer)" title="John Nixon (mining engineer)">John Nixon</a> and partners, Aberfan consisted of two cottages and an inn frequented by local farmers and bargemen.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin19677_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin19677-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOwen201113_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOwen201113-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> By 1966 its population had grown to approximately 5,000, most of whom were employed in the coal industry.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOwen201113_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOwen201113-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbernethy2005113_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbernethy2005113-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Since the <a href="/wiki/Nationalisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Nationalisation">nationalisation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Coal_mining_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Coal mining in the United Kingdom">British coal industry</a> in 1947, Aberfan\'s colliery had been under the control of the <a href="/wiki/National_Coal_Board" title="National Coal Board">National Coal Board</a> (NCB).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin19678_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin19678-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Regulation in the coal industry was provided by <a href="/wiki/HM_Inspectorate_of_Mines" class="mw-redirect" title="HM Inspectorate of Mines">HM Inspectorate of Mines</a>. The inspectors had worked as engineers in the coal industry, and were former employees of the NCB.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200048,_191_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200048,_191-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/River_Taff" title="River Taff">River Taff</a> runs north-to-south through the village; at the upper side of the settlement, on the western outskirts, a disused canal bed and a railway embankment run parallel to the river.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196713_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196713-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin19672\xe2\x80\x933_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin19672\xe2\x80\x933-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first <a href="/wiki/Overburden" title="Overburden">spoil</a> from the coal mine was deposited on the valley\'s lower slopes, east of the canal, but during the 1910s the first tip was started on the western slopes, above the canal line and the village. By 1966 there were seven spoil heaps, comprising approximately 2.6&#160;million&#160;cu&#160;yd (2.0&#160;million&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of waste.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENield2016_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENield2016-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196713,_18_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196713,_18-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> Tips 4 and 5 were conical mounds at the apex of the slope, although Tip 4 was misshapen from an earlier slip; the remaining five were lower down; all were directly above the village. Tip 7 was the only one being used in 1966. About 111 feet (34&#160;m) high, it contained 297,000 cubic yards (227,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of spoil, which included 30,000 cubic yards (23,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of <a href="/wiki/Tailings" title="Tailings">tailings</a>\xe2\x80\x94waste from the chemical extraction of coal, fine particles of coal and ash which took on the similar properties to <a href="/wiki/Quicksand" title="Quicksand">quicksand</a> when wet.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOwen201113_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOwen201113-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin19679_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin19679-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196718_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196718-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000146_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000146-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aberfan_Colliery_spoil_tramway_-_geograph.org.uk_-_73636.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Aberfan_Colliery_spoil_tramway_-_geograph.org.uk_-_73636.jpg/170px-Aberfan_Colliery_spoil_tramway_-_geograph.org.uk_-_73636.jpg" width="170" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Aberfan_Colliery_spoil_tramway_-_geograph.org.uk_-_73636.jpg/255px-Aberfan_Colliery_spoil_tramway_-_geograph.org.uk_-_73636.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Aberfan_Colliery_spoil_tramway_-_geograph.org.uk_-_73636.jpg/340px-Aberfan_Colliery_spoil_tramway_-_geograph.org.uk_-_73636.jpg 2x" data-file-width="422" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aberfan_Colliery_spoil_tramway_-_geograph.org.uk_-_73636.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Aberfan Colliery spoil tramway in 1964, with <a href="/wiki/Spoil_tip" title="Spoil tip">spoil heaps</a> at top left. The <a href="/wiki/Pennant_sandstone" class="mw-redirect" title="Pennant sandstone">pennant sandstone</a> building at mid-left is Pantglas County Secondary School, which lies adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/Junior_school" title="Junior school">junior school</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Tip stability is affected by water conditions. Tips 4, 5 and 7 had been sited on streams or springs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin19679,_10_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin19679,_10-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The presence of the springs was common knowledge in the area, and they had been marked on the <a href="/wiki/Ordnance_Survey" title="Ordnance Survey">Ordnance Survey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geological_Society_of_London" title="Geological Society of London">Geological Society</a> maps since 1874.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200029_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200029-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECouto1989315_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECouto1989315-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Tip 4 at Aberfan, which had been used between 1933 and 1945, was large, and had been started on boggy ground between two streams. At the time of its planning, the Merthyr Tydfil borough engineer thought that despite the position, it would be unlikely to avalanche. Following some ground movements in the tip in the early 1940s, a drainage channel was dug in early 1944. In November that year part of the tip slid 1,600 feet (490&#160;m) down the mountain to stop approximately 500 feet (150&#160;m) above the village.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196718_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196718-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin19678\xe2\x80\x939_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin19678\xe2\x80\x939-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In May 1963 Tip 7 shifted slightly; in November that year there was a more substantial slide. The NCB stated that the movement had not been a "slide", but was instead a "tailings run"\xe2\x80\x94a run-off of tailings from the surface of the tip\xe2\x80\x94which left its stability unaffected. After the slide, the NCB stopped tipping tailings on number 7, but normal spoil continued to be deposited.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196761\xe2\x80\x9362,_64_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196761\xe2\x80\x9362,_64-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Aberfan is in an area of relatively high rainfall, an average of 60 inches (1,500&#160;mm) a year. In 1960 it was 70.5 inches (1,790&#160;mm), the heaviest of recent years in the run-up to the disaster.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin196710_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin196710-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller197422_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller197422-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Between 1952 and 1965, there was severe flooding in the Pantglas area of Aberfan on at least 11 occasions. Residents complained that the flood water was black and left a greasy residue when it receded.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196720_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196720-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Complaints had been made by residents to <a href="/wiki/Merthyr_Tydfil_County_Borough_Council" title="Merthyr Tydfil County Borough Council">Merthyr Tydfil County Borough Council</a>, who corresponded with the NCB between July 1963 and March 1964 on the topic of the "Danger from Coal Slurry being tipped at the rear of the Pantglas Schools".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196755_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196755-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> In early 1965 meetings were held between the council and the NCB at which the Board agreed to take action on the clogged pipes and drainage ditches that were the cause of the flooding. No action had been taken by October 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196722_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196722-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tip_collapse">Tip collapse</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aberfan_disaster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Tip collapse">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>During the first three weeks of October 1966 there was 6.5 inches (170&#160;mm) of rainfall, nearly half of which was in the third week.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin196710_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin196710-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> During the night of 20\xe2\x80\x9321 October the peak of Tip 7 subsided by 9\xe2\x80\x9310 feet (2.7\xe2\x80\x933.0&#160;m) and the rails on which the spoil was transported to the top of the tip fell into the resulting hole. The spoil movement was discovered at 7:30<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>am by the first members of the morning shift manning the heaps. One of the workers walked to the colliery to report the slip; he returned with the supervisor for the tips, and it was decided that no further work would be done that day, but that a new tipping position would be decided on the following week.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENield2016_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENield2016-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller197425\xe2\x80\x9326_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller197425\xe2\x80\x9326-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin196713\xe2\x80\x9314_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin196713\xe2\x80\x9314-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aberfan_disaster_map_-_extent_of_the_spoil_slip.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Aberfan_disaster_map_-_extent_of_the_spoil_slip.jpg/220px-Aberfan_disaster_map_-_extent_of_the_spoil_slip.jpg" width="220" height="366" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Aberfan_disaster_map_-_extent_of_the_spoil_slip.jpg/330px-Aberfan_disaster_map_-_extent_of_the_spoil_slip.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Aberfan_disaster_map_-_extent_of_the_spoil_slip.jpg/440px-Aberfan_disaster_map_-_extent_of_the_spoil_slip.jpg 2x" data-file-width="890" data-file-height="1479" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aberfan_disaster_map_-_extent_of_the_spoil_slip.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map from the 1967 inquiry report, showing the extent of the spoil spill (stippled, within dotted lines)</div></div></div>\n<p>At 9:15<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>am a significant amount of <a href="/wiki/Soil_liquefaction" title="Soil liquefaction">water-saturated debris</a> broke away from tip 7 and flowed downhill at 11\xe2\x80\x9321 miles per hour (18\xe2\x80\x9334&#160;km/h) in waves 20\xe2\x80\x9330 feet (6.1\xe2\x80\x939.1&#160;m) high.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup> G. M. J. Williams, a consultant engineer who gave evidence at the subsequent tribunal, stated that the 9:15&#160;am movement:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>took part of the saturated material past the point where liquefaction occurred. This initially liquefied material began to move rapidly, releasing energy which liquefied the rest of the saturated portion of the tip, and almost instantaneously the nature of the saturated lower parts of Tip No. 7 was changed from that of a solid to that of a heavy liquid of a density of approximately twice that of water. This was \'the dark glistening wave\' which several witnesses saw burst from the bottom of the tip.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196726\xe2\x80\x9327_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196726\xe2\x80\x9327-33">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>Approximately 140,000 cubic yards (110,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of spoil slid 700 yards (640&#160;m) down the mountain, destroying two farm cottages and killing the occupants. Around 50,000 cubic yards (38,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) travelled across the canal and railway embankment and into the village.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196726_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196726-34">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPetley2016_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPetley2016-35">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGriffiths1983271_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGriffiths1983271-36">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The flow destroyed two <a href="/wiki/Water_mains" class="mw-redirect" title="Water mains">water mains</a> buried in the embankment and the additional water further saturated the spoil.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin196718\xe2\x80\x9319_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin196718\xe2\x80\x9319-37">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Those who heard the avalanche said the sound reminded them of a low-flying jet or thunder.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196727_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196727-38">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The avalanche struck Pantglas Junior School on Moy Road, demolishing and engulfing much of the structure and filling classrooms with thick mud, sludge and rubble; 109 children were killed in the school, from 240 attendees, and five teachers. The pupils of Pantglas Junior School had arrived only minutes earlier for the last day before the half-term holiday, which was due to start at 12.00&#160;pm. The teachers had just begun to record the children\'s attendance in the registers when the landslide hit.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin196715,_19\xe2\x80\x9321_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin196715,_19\xe2\x80\x9321-39">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The adjacent secondary school was also damaged, and 18 houses on surrounding roads were destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196726_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196726-34">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Mud and water from the slide flooded other houses in the vicinity, forcing many to evacuate their homes. Once the slide material had come to a halt, it re-solidified.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;d&#93;</a></sup> A huge mound of slurry up to 30 feet (9.1&#160;m) high blocked the area.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196728_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196728-31">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLean200949_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLean200949-41">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams196993_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams196993-42">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The acting headmaster of the secondary school recalled:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>The Girls\' Entrance [of the secondary school] was approximately two-thirds to three-quarters full of rubble and waste material&#160;... I climbed onto the rubble in the doorway&#160;... when I looked directly in front of me&#160;... I saw that the houses in Moy Road had vanished in a mass of tip-waste material and that the Junior School gable-ends, or part of the roof, were sticking up out of this morass. I looked down to my right and I saw that the Moy Road houses had gone.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196727\xe2\x80\x9328_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196727\xe2\x80\x9328-43">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>Some staff died trying to protect the children. Nansi Williams, the school meals clerk, used her body to shield five children, who all survived; Williams did not, and was found by rescuers still holding a pound note she had been collecting as lunch money.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin196734_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin196734-44">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Dai Benyon, the deputy headmaster, tried to use a blackboard to shield himself and five children from the slurry pouring through the school. He and all 34 pupils in his class were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin196719_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin196719-45">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> When the avalanche stopped, so did the noise; one resident recalled that "in that silence you couldn\'t hear a bird or a child".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes20003_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes20003-46">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rescue_efforts_and_retrieval_of_the_bodies">Rescue efforts and retrieval of the bodies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aberfan_disaster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Rescue efforts and retrieval of the bodies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rescue_at_Aberfan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8d/Rescue_at_Aberfan.jpg/220px-Rescue_at_Aberfan.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8d/Rescue_at_Aberfan.jpg/330px-Rescue_at_Aberfan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/8d/Rescue_at_Aberfan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="350" data-file-height="233" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rescue_at_Aberfan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The rescue of a young girl from the school; no survivors were found after 11:00&#160;am</div></div></div>\n<p>After the landslide stopped, local residents rushed to the school and began digging through the rubble, moving material by hand or with garden tools.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin196729_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin196729-47">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> At 9:25&#160;am Merthyr Tydfil police received a phone call from a local resident who said "I have been asked to inform that there has been a landslide at Pantglas. The tip has come down on the school";<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;South_Wales_Police_Museum&quot;2_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;South_Wales_Police_Museum&quot;2-48">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Fire_brigade" class="mw-redirect" title="Fire brigade">fire brigade</a>, based in Merthyr Tydfil, received a call at about the same time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin196726_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin196726-49">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Calls were then made to local hospitals, the ambulance service and the local <a href="/wiki/Civil_Defence_Corps" title="Civil Defence Corps">Civil Defence Corps</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller197427_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller197427-50">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The first miners from the Aberfan colliery arrived within 20 minutes of the disaster, having been raised from the coal seams where they had been working. They directed the early digging, knowing that unplanned excavation could lead to collapse of the spoil and the remnants of the buildings; they worked in organised groups under the control of their pit managers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller197427_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller197427-50">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin196734,_48_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin196734,_48-51">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first casualties from the wreckage of the school arrived at <a href="/wiki/St_Tydfil%27s_Hospital" title="St Tydfil&#39;s Hospital">St Tydfil\'s Hospital</a> in Merthyr Tydfil at 9.50&#160;am; the remaining rescued casualties all arrived before 11.00&#160;am: 22 children, one of whom was dead on arrival, and 5 adults. A further 9 casualties were sent to the <a href="/wiki/East_Glamorgan_General_Hospital" class="mw-redirect" title="East Glamorgan General Hospital">East Glamorgan General Hospital</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin196736,_223_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin196736,_223-52">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> No survivors were found after 11.00&#160;am. Of the 144 people who died in the disaster, 116 were children, mostly between the ages of 7 and 10; 109 of the children died inside Pantglas Junior School. Five of the adults who died were teachers at the school. An additional 6 adults and 29 children were injured.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196726_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196726-34">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 10:30&#160;am BBC news summary led with the story of the accident. The result was that thousands of volunteers travelled to Aberfan to help, although their efforts often hampered the work of the experienced miners or trained rescue teams.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin196749_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin196749-53">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:264px;max-width:264px"><div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">Aerial photographs of the spoil tips above Aberfan before and after the disaster</div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:262px;max-width:262px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Aberfan_spoil_heaps_pre_disaster.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Aberfan_spoil_heaps_pre_disaster.jpg/260px-Aberfan_spoil_heaps_pre_disaster.jpg" width="260" height="161" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Aberfan_spoil_heaps_pre_disaster.jpg/390px-Aberfan_spoil_heaps_pre_disaster.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Aberfan_spoil_heaps_pre_disaster.jpg/520px-Aberfan_spoil_heaps_pre_disaster.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1301" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Before the slip</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:262px;max-width:262px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Aberfan_spoil_heaps_post_disaster.tif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Aberfan_spoil_heaps_post_disaster.tif/lossy-page1-260px-Aberfan_spoil_heaps_post_disaster.tif.jpg" width="260" height="159" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Aberfan_spoil_heaps_post_disaster.tif/lossy-page1-390px-Aberfan_spoil_heaps_post_disaster.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Aberfan_spoil_heaps_post_disaster.tif/lossy-page1-520px-Aberfan_spoil_heaps_post_disaster.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1282" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">After the slip</div></div></div></div>\n<p>With the two broken water mains still pumping water into the spoil in Aberfan, the slip continued to move through the village, and it was not until 11:30&#160;am that the water authorities managed to turn off the supply.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;e&#93;</a></sup> It was estimated that the mains added between 2 and 3&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Imperial_gallon" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial gallon">imperial gallons</a> (9\xe2\x80\x9314&#160;million litres) of water to the spoil slurry.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin196739\xe2\x80\x9340_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin196739\xe2\x80\x9340-54">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> With movement in the upper slopes still a danger, at 12:00&#160;noon NCB engineers began digging a drainage channel, with the aim of stabilising the tip. It took two hours to reroute the water to a safer place, from where it was diverted into an existing water course.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin196740\xe2\x80\x9341_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin196740\xe2\x80\x9341-56">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>An NCB board meeting that morning, headed by the organisation\'s chairman, <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Robens,_Baron_Robens_of_Woldingham" title="Alfred Robens, Baron Robens of Woldingham">Lord Robens</a>, was informed of the disaster. It was decided that the company\'s Director-General of Production and its Chief Safety Engineer should inspect the situation, and they left for the village immediately.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin196763_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin196763-57">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> In his autobiography, Robens stated that the decision for him not to go was because "the appearance of a layman at too early a stage inevitably distracts senior and essential people from the tasks upon which they should be exclusively concentrating".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobens1972247_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobens1972247-58">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Instead of visiting the scene, that evening Robens went to the ceremony to invest him as the chancellor of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Surrey" title="University of Surrey">University of Surrey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETweedale2004_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETweedale2004-59">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> NCB officers covered up for him when contacted by <a href="/wiki/Cledwyn_Hughes,_Baron_Cledwyn_of_Penrhos" title="Cledwyn Hughes, Baron Cledwyn of Penrhos">Cledwyn Hughes</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Wales" title="Secretary of State for Wales">Secretary of State for Wales</a>, falsely claiming that Robens was personally directing relief work.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200023_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200023-60">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hughes visited the scene at 4:00&#160;pm for an hour. He telephoned <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister</a>, and confirmed Wilson\'s own thought that he should also visit.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin196745,_58_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin196745,_58-61">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Wilson told Hughes to "take whatever action he thought necessary, irrespective of any considerations of \'normal procedures\', expenditure or statutory limitations".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJohnson19661_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJohnson19661-62">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Wilson arrived at Aberfan at 9.40&#160;pm, where he heard reports from the police and civil defence forces, and visited the rescue workers. Before he left, at midnight, he and Hughes agreed that a high-level independent inquiry needed to be held.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin196768\xe2\x80\x9369_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin196768\xe2\x80\x9369-63">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> That evening the mayor of Merthyr Tydfil launched an appeal for financial donations\xe2\x80\x94soon formally named the Aberfan Disaster Fund\xe2\x80\x94to alleviate financial hardship and to help rebuild the area.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller197429_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller197429-64">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A makeshift mortuary was set up in the village\'s Bethania Chapel on 21&#160;October and operated until 4&#160;November, 250 yards (229&#160;m) from the disaster site; members of the <a href="/wiki/South_Wales_Police" title="South Wales Police">South Wales Police</a> force assisted with the identification and registration of the victims. Two doctors examined the bodies and issued death certificates; the cause of death was typically <a href="/wiki/Asphyxia" title="Asphyxia">asphyxia</a>, fractured skull or multiple crush injuries. Cramped conditions in the chapel meant that parents could only be admitted one at a time to identify the bodies of their children. The building also acted as a missing persons bureau and its vestry was used by <a href="/wiki/Red_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Cross">Red Cross</a> volunteers and <a href="/wiki/St_John_Ambulance" title="St John Ambulance">St John Ambulance</a> stretcher-bearers. Four hundred embalmers volunteered to assist with the cleaning and dressing of the corpses; a contingent that flew over from Northern Ireland removed the seats of their plane to transport child-sized coffins. The smaller Aberfan Calvinistic Chapel nearby was used as a second mortuary from 22 to 29 October.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;South_Wales_Police_Museum&quot;2\xe2\x80\x933_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;South_Wales_Police_Museum&quot;2\xe2\x80\x933-65">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWroe2016_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWroe2016-66">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENunn19872069_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENunn19872069-67">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the morning of Saturday 22&#160;October, 111 bodies had been excavated, of which 51 had been identified. At daybreak the <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen\'s</a> brother-in-law <a href="/wiki/Antony_Armstrong-Jones,_1st_Earl_of_Snowdon" title="Antony Armstrong-Jones, 1st Earl of Snowdon">Lord Snowdon</a> visited and spoke with workers and parents; at 11:00&#160;am <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip,_Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh">Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh</a>, visited the scene and talked to rescue workers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin196780\xe2\x80\x9381_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin196780\xe2\x80\x9381-68">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> In the early afternoon light rain began falling, which became increasingly heavy; it caused further movement in the tip, which threatened the rescue work and raised the possibility that the area would have to be evacuated.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClarkRoad19661_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClarkRoad19661-69">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Robens arrived in Aberfan on Saturday evening. After visiting the colliery and the disaster site, he gave a press conference at which he stated that the NCB would work with any public inquiry. In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i>, Robens said the organisation "will not seek to hide behind any legal loophole or make any legal quibble about responsibility".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;No_hiding_by_the_Coal_Board&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Observer&#39;&#39;_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;No_hiding_by_the_Coal_Board&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Observer&#39;&#39;-70">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Robens returned to the village the following morning to see the situation in daylight. He was interviewed by a television news team while examining the tip. When asked about the responsibility of the NCB for the slide, he answered:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>I wouldn\'t have thought myself that anybody would know that there was a spring deep in the heart of a mountain, any more than I can tell you there is one under our feet where we are now. If you are asking me did any of my people on the spot know that there was this spring water, then the answer is, No\xe2\x80\x94they couldn\'t possibly.&#160;... It was impossible to know that there was a spring in the heart of this tip which was turning the centre of the mountain into sludge.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobens1972250\xe2\x80\x93251_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobens1972250\xe2\x80\x93251-71">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mynwent_Aberfan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Mynwent_Aberfan.jpg/220px-Mynwent_Aberfan.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Mynwent_Aberfan.jpg/330px-Mynwent_Aberfan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Mynwent_Aberfan.jpg/440px-Mynwent_Aberfan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mynwent_Aberfan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The white arches in Bryntaf Cemetery, Aberfan, which mark the graves of children killed in the disaster.</div></div></div>\n<p>On 23 October assistance was provided by the <a href="/wiki/Army_Reserve_(United_Kingdom)" title="Army Reserve (United Kingdom)">Territorial Army</a>. This was followed by the arrival of naval ratings from <a href="/wiki/HMS_Tiger_(C20)" title="HMS Tiger (C20)">HMS&#160;<i>Tiger</i></a> and members of the <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Own_Royal_Border_Regiment" title="King&#39;s Own Royal Border Regiment">King\'s Own Royal Border Regiment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin1967118\xe2\x80\x93119,_225_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin1967118\xe2\x80\x93119,_225-72">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> That day Wilson announced the appointment of <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Appeal_judge_(England_and_Wales)" title="Court of Appeal judge (England and Wales)">Lord Justice</a> <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Davies,_Baron_Edmund-Davies" title="Edmund Davies, Baron Edmund-Davies">Edmund Davies</a> as the chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Aberfan_Disaster_Tribunal" title="Aberfan Disaster Tribunal">inquiry into the disaster</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;Welsh_Judge_to_Head_Aberfan_Inquiry&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Times&#39;&#39;_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;Welsh_Judge_to_Head_Aberfan_Inquiry&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Times&#39;&#39;-73">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Davies had been born and schooled in the nearby village of <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Ash,_Rhondda_Cynon_Taf" title="Mountain Ash, Rhondda Cynon Taf">Mountain Ash</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200023_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200023-60">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;Edmund-Davies,_Baron&quot;,_Who&#39;s_Who_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;Edmund-Davies,_Baron&quot;,_Who&#39;s_Who-74">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Inquests_in_England_and_Wales" title="Inquests in England and Wales">coroner\'s inquest</a> was opened on 24 October to give the causes of death for 30 of the children located. One man who lost his wife and two sons called out when he heard their names mentioned: "No, sir\xe2\x80\x94buried alive by the National Coal Board"; one woman shouted that the NCB had "killed our children".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrost19661_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrost19661-75">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The first funerals, for five of the children, took place the following day.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrost196616_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrost196616-76">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> A mass funeral for 81 children and one woman took place at Bryntaf Cemetery in Aberfan on 27 October. They were buried in a pair of 80-foot-long (24&#160;m) trenches; 10,000 people attended.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;Welsh_Valleys_Mourn_the_Children_of_Aberfan&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Times&#39;&#39;_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;Welsh_Valleys_Mourn_the_Children_of_Aberfan&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Times&#39;&#39;-77">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Because of the vast quantity and consistency of the spoil, it was a week before all the bodies were recovered; the last victim was found on 28&#160;October.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200023_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200023-60">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin1967226_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin1967226-78">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;f&#93;</a></sup> The Queen and the Duke of Edinburgh visited Aberfan on 29&#160;October to pay their respects to those who had died. Their visit coincided with the end of the main rescue phase; only one contracting firm remained in the village to continue the last stages of the clear-up.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;Peace_Returns_To_Aberfan&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Times&#39;&#39;_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;Peace_Returns_To_Aberfan&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Times&#39;&#39;-80">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aberfan_disaster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aberfan_Disaster_Tribunal">Aberfan Disaster Tribunal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aberfan_disaster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Aberfan Disaster Tribunal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Aberfan_Disaster_Tribunal" title="Aberfan Disaster Tribunal">Aberfan Disaster Tribunal</a></div>\n<p>On 25 October 1966, after resolutions in both Houses of Parliament, the Secretary of State for Wales formally appointed a tribunal to inquire into the disaster.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;Aberfan_Inquiry_Powers&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Times&#39;&#39;_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;Aberfan_Inquiry_Powers&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Times&#39;&#39;-81">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Before the tribunal began, the <a href="/wiki/Attorney_General_for_England_and_Wales" title="Attorney General for England and Wales">Attorney General</a> cautioned the media that commenting on matters to be investigated by the tribunal could lay them open to the same consequences as <a href="/wiki/Contempt_of_court" title="Contempt of court">contempt of court</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJones19661315\xe2\x80\x931320_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJones19661315\xe2\x80\x931320-82">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;g&#93;</a></sup> Sitting alongside Lord Justice Davies on the inquiry were the civil engineer <a href="/wiki/Harold_Harding" title="Harold Harding">Harold Harding</a> and Vernon Lawrence, the former Clerk to the <a href="/wiki/Monmouthshire_County_Council" title="Monmouthshire County Council">Monmouthshire County Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHowe1968107_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHowe1968107-84">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The inquiry had an initial public meeting on 2 November 1966 and took evidence in public for 76 days, spread over the next five months; during that time 136 witnesses testified.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies19677_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies19677-85">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin1967192\xe2\x80\x93193_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin1967192\xe2\x80\x93193-86">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The tribunal report thought "much of the time of the Tribunal could have been saved if&#160;... the National Coal Board had not stubbornly resisted every attempt to lay the blame where it so clearly must rest\xe2\x80\x94at their door".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196789_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196789-87">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Aberfan\'s MP, <a href="/wiki/S._O._Davies" title="S. O. Davies">S. O. Davies</a>, gave evidence to the tribunal and stated that he had long held concerns that the tip "might not only slide, but in sliding might reach the village"; he added that he had not spoken out because he had "more than a shrewd suspicion that that colliery would be closed".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196733_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196733-88">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Brian Gibbens, <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Counsel" title="Queen&#39;s Counsel">QC</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Counsel" title="Counsel">counsel</a> for the <a href="/wiki/National_Union_of_Mineworkers_(Great_Britain)" title="National Union of Mineworkers (Great Britain)">National Union of Mineworkers</a> (NUM), challenged Davies\'s evidence and stated that if the testament "is to be accepted as truthful and accurate in his recollection&#160;... then he bears what must be one of the largest personal burdens of responsibility for the disaster".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196733_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196733-88">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Gibbens requested that Davies\'s testimony be rejected, on the basis that he "never appreciated what in fact was the import of his words".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196734_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196734-89">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The tribunal agreed, and stated that "we doubt that he fully understood the grave implication of what he was saying".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196734_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196734-89">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Initially the tribunal decided not to call Robens to testify\xe2\x80\x94they took his comment to the media about the existence of the spring being unknown as hearsay, and thought that his evidence could not help. The counsel for the families, <a href="/wiki/Desmond_Ackner,_Baron_Ackner" title="Desmond Ackner, Baron Ackner">Desmond Ackner</a>, QC, attacked Robens for making the statement about the spring, saying it was "a public scandal"; he added that "at no stage throughout this Inquiry has the National Coal Board taken the initiative to correct this sentence". Ackner also criticised Robens\'s absence from the inquiry, saying that "no explanation has been proffered by or on behalf of Lord Robens and his absence, therefore, and in this regard has been conspicuous."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196790_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196790-90">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The tribunal members decided that Robens should be able to defend his position and he was invited to attend. Under <a href="/wiki/Cross-examination" title="Cross-examination">cross-examination</a> by Ackner, Robens gave evidence inconsistent with that provided by the NCB, particularly on the point of whether the disaster was foreseeable; counsel for the organisation asked the tribunal to ignore Robens\'s testimony.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196791\xe2\x80\x9392_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196791\xe2\x80\x9392-91">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The tribunal concluded its hearings on 28 April 1967 and published its report on 3 August. Among their findings was that "[b]lame for the disaster rests upon the National Coal Board.&#160;... This blame is shared (though in varying degrees) among the National Coal Board headquarters, the South Western Divisional Board, and certain individuals."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies1967131_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies1967131-92">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> They added that the "legal liability of the National Coal Board to pay compensation for the personal injuries (fatal or otherwise) and damage to property is incontestable and uncontested".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies1967131_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies1967131-92">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> In its introduction the inquiry team wrote that it was their\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>strong and unanimous view&#160;... that the Aberfan disaster could and should have been prevented.&#160;... the Report which follows tells not of wickedness but of ignorance, ineptitude and a failure in communications. Ignorance on the part of those charged at all levels with the siting, control and daily management of tips; bungling ineptitude on the part of those who had the duty of supervising and directing them; and failure on the part of those having knowledge of the factors which affect tip safety to communicate that knowledge and to see that it was applied.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196711_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196711-93">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>Nine employees of the NCB were censured by the inquiry, with "many degrees of blameworthiness, from very slight to grave", although McLean and Johnes consider that some senior staff whom the evidence shows to have been culpable were omitted, and one junior member of staff named in the report should not have been blamed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196792\xe2\x80\x93107_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196792\xe2\x80\x93107-94">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200039\xe2\x80\x9343_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200039\xe2\x80\x9343-95">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;h&#93;</a></sup> The tribunal decided that no blame lay with Merthyr Tydfil County Borough Council or the NUM.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies1967109\xe2\x80\x93110,_112_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies1967109\xe2\x80\x93110,_112-106">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The tribunal made several recommendations, including the need for the extension of the Mines and Quarries Act 1954 to cover tips, and the formation of a National Tip Safety Committee to advise the government. The inquiry report also advised that "action needs to be taken to safeguard the future condition of the tips at Aberfan".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies1967131\xe2\x80\x93132_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies1967131\xe2\x80\x93132-107">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The sociologist Barry Turner, in a 1976 study, identified several errors that led to the Aberfan disaster. These included years of rigid and unrealistic disregard for the importance of the safety of the above-ground tips (as opposed to dangers within the mines);<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner1976392_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner1976392-108">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> a flawed decision-making process which ignored or minimised the likelihood and the scale of the emergent danger; a dismissive attitude toward the complaints from Aberfan residents, discounting the validity of their concerns;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner1976385,_393_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner1976385,_393-109">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> and an incomplete and inadequate response to conditions which caused those complaints.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurner1976388\xe2\x80\x93389_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurner1976388\xe2\x80\x93389-110">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>McLean and Johnes observe that HM Inspectorate of Mines went largely unchallenged by the tribunal, although the two consider that the organisation failed in their duty; in doing so, they created a situation of <a href="/wiki/Regulatory_capture" title="Regulatory capture">regulatory capture</a>, where rather than protecting the public interest\xe2\x80\x94in this case the citizens of Aberfan\xe2\x80\x94their regulatory failures fell in line with the interests of the NCB, the organisation they were supposed to be overseeing.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200048,_190_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200048,_190-111">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aberfan_residents">Aberfan residents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aberfan_disaster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Aberfan residents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Merthyr_Vale_Aberfan_Aberdare_Blog.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Merthyr_Vale_Aberfan_Aberdare_Blog.jpg/220px-Merthyr_Vale_Aberfan_Aberdare_Blog.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Merthyr_Vale_Aberfan_Aberdare_Blog.jpg/330px-Merthyr_Vale_Aberfan_Aberdare_Blog.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Merthyr_Vale_Aberfan_Aberdare_Blog.jpg/440px-Merthyr_Vale_Aberfan_Aberdare_Blog.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Merthyr_Vale_Aberfan_Aberdare_Blog.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aberfan in 2007; the cemetery is visible in the centre of the picture</div></div></div>\n<p>During the rescue, the shock and grief of parents and villagers was exacerbated by insensitive behaviour from the media\xe2\x80\x94one rescue worker recalled hearing a press photographer asking a child to cry for her dead friends because it would make a good picture.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWatkins198614_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWatkins198614-112">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The response of the general public in donating to the memorial fund, together with over 50,000 letters of condolence that accompanied many of the donations, helped many residents come to terms with the disaster. One bereaved mother said "People all over the world felt for us. We knew that with their letters and the contributions they sent&#160;... They helped us build a better Aberfan."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000111\xe2\x80\x93112_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000111\xe2\x80\x93112-113">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A study published in the <i><a href="/wiki/British_Journal_of_Psychiatry" title="British Journal of Psychiatry">British Journal of Psychiatry</a></i> (BJP) in 2003 found that half the survivors of the disaster had experienced <a href="/wiki/Post-traumatic_stress_disorder" class="mw-redirect" title="Post-traumatic stress disorder">post-traumatic stress disorder</a> (PTSD) at some time in their lives, that they were more than three times more likely to have developed lifetime PTSD than a comparison group of individuals who had experienced other life-threatening traumas, and that 34 per cent of survivors who took part in the study reported that they still experienced bad dreams or difficulty sleeping because of intrusive thoughts about the disaster.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorganScourfieldWilliamsJasper2003532,_533_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorganScourfieldWilliamsJasper2003532,_533-114">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> In 2005 <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Tobacco" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Tobacco">Imperial Tobacco</a> settled out of court to end an <a href="/wiki/Unfair_dismissal_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Unfair dismissal in the United Kingdom">unfair dismissal</a> suit brought against the company by an Aberfan survivor, who had been employed by the company\'s <a href="/wiki/Rizla" title="Rizla">Rizla</a> cigarette paper factory near <a href="/wiki/Pontypridd" title="Pontypridd">Pontypridd</a>. She had been sacked after she refused to continue working night shifts, stating that it had brought on flashbacks from 1966, when she had been buried waist-deep in the landslide while walking to school. She survived, but a friend who had been walking with her was killed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;&#39;Aberfan_Trauma&#39;_Case_Settled&quot;,_BBC_News_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;&#39;Aberfan_Trauma&#39;_Case_Settled&quot;,_BBC_News-115">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The BJP study also found that there was no significant rise in the risk of <a href="/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">depression</a> or <a href="/wiki/Substance_abuse" title="Substance abuse">substance abuse</a> in survivors.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorganScourfieldWilliamsJasper2003532,_533_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorganScourfieldWilliamsJasper2003532,_533-114">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Some parents of deceased children reported <a href="/wiki/Survivor_guilt" title="Survivor guilt">extreme feelings of guilt</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller197494_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller197494-116">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> as did one of the pupils who survived, who reported:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>There was none of the discipline we used to have&#160;... We didn\'t go out to play for a long time because those who\'d lost their own children couldn\'t bear to see us. We all knew what they were feeling and we felt guilty about being alive.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLean,_Iain._&quot;The_Last_Day_Before_Half-Term&quot;_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLean,_Iain._&quot;The_Last_Day_Before_Half-Term&quot;-117">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>The residents of Aberfan experienced medical problems after the disaster. Many survivors reported suffering from "sleeping difficulties, nervousness, lack of friends, unwillingness to go to school and <a href="/wiki/Enuresis" title="Enuresis">enuresis</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorganScourfieldWilliamsJasper2003532_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorganScourfieldWilliamsJasper2003532-118">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> In the year following the tip slide, close relatives of the victims had a death rate seven times higher than the norm.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilkinson2002180_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilkinson2002180-119">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> One local doctor later wrote "By every statistic, patients seen, prescriptions written, deaths, I can prove that this is a village of excessive sickness."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLean,_Iain._&quot;The_Last_Day_Before_Half-Term&quot;_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLean,_Iain._&quot;The_Last_Day_Before_Half-Term&quot;-117">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Despite these problems, during the five years after the disaster the birth rate rose considerably, in marked contrast to that of Merthyr Tydfil.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliamsParkes1975303_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliamsParkes1975303-120">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="NCB_and_its_personnel">NCB and its personnel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aberfan_disaster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: NCB and its personnel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The NCB as an organisation was not prosecuted,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;i&#93;</a></sup> and no NCB staff were demoted, sacked or prosecuted as a consequence of the Aberfan disaster or for evidence given to the inquiry.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLean2007_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLean2007-124">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> During a parliamentary debate on the disaster, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a>\xe2\x80\x94then the opposition spokesman on power\xe2\x80\x94raised the situation of one witness, criticised by the inquiry, who had subsequently been promoted to a board-level position at the NCB by the time the report was published.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThatcher19671991\xe2\x80\x931996_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThatcher19671991\xe2\x80\x931996-125">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200026_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200026-126">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2000 Iain McLean, a professor of politics, and Martin Johnes, a research fellow in Welsh history, undertook a study of the Aberfan disaster and its repercussions; their work included government papers released in 1997 under the <a href="/wiki/Thirty-year_rule" title="Thirty-year rule">thirty-year rule</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000viii_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000viii-127">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Their opinion is that "the Coal Board \'<a href="/wiki/Spin_(propaganda)" title="Spin (propaganda)">spin-doctored</a>\' its way out of trouble, controlling the public agenda from the day of the disaster until the tips were finally removed".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200026_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200026-126">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Robens had received a copy of the inquiry report ten days before its official publication and began a campaign to strengthen his position. He went on a tour of British coalfields, giving speeches that promoted the use of coal and criticised the increasing popularity of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear power</a>. All messages of support to him were catalogued by the NCB, and copies of some were leaked to the press;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLean200950\xe2\x80\x9351_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLean200950\xe2\x80\x9351-128">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> the manoeuvring led to criticism in an editorial in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, which stated that "the Coal Board\'s behaviour has&#160;... been rather unseemly in the circumstances".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;Is_it_a_Resigning_Matter?&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Guardian&#39;&#39;_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;Is_it_a_Resigning_Matter?&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Guardian&#39;&#39;-129">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 1967\xe2\x80\x94following the publication of the inquiry report\xe2\x80\x94Robens discussed his position with the Minister of Power, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Marsh,_Baron_Marsh" title="Richard Marsh, Baron Marsh">Richard Marsh</a>. After receiving assurances that his role at the NCB was secure, he offered to resign; in line with the agreement between the two men, the offer was rejected.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLean2007_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLean2007-124">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;Lord_Robens&#39;s_offer_to_resign_not_accepted_yet&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Guardian&#39;&#39;_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;Lord_Robens&#39;s_offer_to_resign_not_accepted_yet&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Guardian&#39;&#39;-130">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> In parliament, the Welsh MP <a href="/wiki/Leo_Abse" title="Leo Abse">Leo Abse</a> said that "when I saw what I regarded as the graceless <a href="/wiki/Pavane" title="Pavane">pavane</a> danced by Lord Robens and the Minister, as the Chairman of the Coal Board coyly offered his resignation and, equally coyly, the Minister rejected the offer, I thought that it was a disgraceful spectacle".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbse19671976\xe2\x80\x931983_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbse19671976\xe2\x80\x931983-131">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Initially the NCB offered bereaved families \xc2\xa350 in compensation, but this was raised to \xc2\xa3500 for each bereaved family;<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;j&#93;</a></sup> the organisation called the amount "a good offer". Many families thought the amount insufficient and petitioned the NCB for an increase; NCB insurance staff advised Robens that "it is only the hard core [of bereaved parents] who are trying to capitalize".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLean2007_124-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLean2007-124">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000161_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000161-134">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Aberfan:_The_Fight_for_Justice&#39;&#39;,_18_October_2016Event_occurs_at_40:35\xe2\x80\x9340:50_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Aberfan:_The_Fight_for_Justice&#39;&#39;,_18_October_2016Event_occurs_at_40:35\xe2\x80\x9340:50-135">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disaster_fund">Disaster fund</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aberfan_disaster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Disaster fund">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The fund set up by the mayor of Merthyr Tydfil grew rapidly, and within a few months nearly 88,000 contributions had been received, totalling \xc2\xa31,606,929; the final total raised was \xc2\xa31.75&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200023,_111\xe2\x80\x93112_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200023,_111\xe2\x80\x93112-136">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;Aberfan_Disaster_\xe2\x80\x93_Financial_Support_for_Individuals&quot;,_Cabinet_Office_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;Aberfan_Disaster_\xe2\x80\x93_Financial_Support_for_Individuals&quot;,_Cabinet_Office-137">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;k&#93;</a></sup> No specific aims for the fund had been outlined by the mayor until it was put on a firm legal footing under the auspices of a permanent committee with clear local representation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes1999382\xe2\x80\x93383_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes1999382\xe2\x80\x93383-139">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> They drew up a deed that outlined the purposes of the fund as:\n</p>\n<blockquote>\n<ol><li>For the relief of all persons who have suffered as a result of the said disaster and are thereby in need.</li>\n<li>Subject as aforesaid for any charitable purpose for the benefit of persons who were inhabitants of Aberfan and its immediate neighbourhood (hereinafter called "the area of benefit") on the 21st day of October 1966 or now are or hereafter become inhabitants of the area of benefit and in particular (but without prejudice to the generality of the last foregoing trust) for any charitable purpose for the benefit of children who were on the 21st day of October 1966 or who now are or hereafter may become resident in the area of benefit.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;Aberfan_Disaster_\xe2\x80\x93_Financial_Support_for_Individuals&quot;,_Cabinet_Office_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;Aberfan_Disaster_\xe2\x80\x93_Financial_Support_for_Individuals&quot;,_Cabinet_Office-137">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup></li></ol></blockquote>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aberfan_Memorial_Garden_dedication_plaque_-_3031769_afe588eb.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Aberfan_Memorial_Garden_dedication_plaque_-_3031769_afe588eb.jpg/240px-Aberfan_Memorial_Garden_dedication_plaque_-_3031769_afe588eb.jpg" width="240" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Aberfan_Memorial_Garden_dedication_plaque_-_3031769_afe588eb.jpg/360px-Aberfan_Memorial_Garden_dedication_plaque_-_3031769_afe588eb.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Aberfan_Memorial_Garden_dedication_plaque_-_3031769_afe588eb.jpg/480px-Aberfan_Memorial_Garden_dedication_plaque_-_3031769_afe588eb.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="356" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aberfan_Memorial_Garden_dedication_plaque_-_3031769_afe588eb.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The dedication plaque at the Aberfan Memorial Garden</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1967 the <a href="/wiki/Charity_Commission_for_England_and_Wales" title="Charity Commission for England and Wales">Charity Commission</a> advised that any money paid to the parents of bereaved families would be against the terms of the trust deed. After arguments from lawyers for the trust, they agreed that there was an "unprecedented emotional state" surrounding Aberfan, and suggested that sums of no more than \xc2\xa3500 should be paid. Members of the trust told the commission that \xc2\xa35,000 was to be paid to each family; the commission agreed that the amount was permissible, but stated that each case should be examined before payment "to ascertain whether the parents had been close to their children and were thus likely to be suffering mentally", according to one member of the Charity Commission.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes1999384\xe2\x80\x93386_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes1999384\xe2\x80\x93386-140">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000140_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000140-141">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> In November 1967 the commission threatened to remove trustees of the disaster fund or make a financial order against them if they made grants to parents of children who were physically uninjured but who were suffering mentally\xe2\x80\x94some surviving children complained of being afraid of the dark and loud noises, while some refused to sleep alone; the commission informed them that any payments would be "quite illegal".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000141_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000141-142">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;How_Close_Were_you_to_your_Dead_Child?&quot;,_&#39;&#39;Times_Higher_Education_Supplement&#39;&#39;_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;How_Close_Were_you_to_your_Dead_Child?&quot;,_&#39;&#39;Times_Higher_Education_Supplement&#39;&#39;-143">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> The decision affected 340 physically uninjured children.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller197447_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller197447-144">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other grants made by the trust were less controversial: for those who lost their house, or whose property suffered significant damage, the trust donated \xc2\xa3100 to assist with evacuation, and additional funds to help replace damaged effects.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller197448_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller197448-145">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;l&#93;</a></sup> \xc2\xa3100,000 was set aside for the future needs of the eight children physically injured in the disaster, and \xc2\xa35,000 was placed in trust for them for when they came of age.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller197447_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller197447-144">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;m&#93;</a></sup> The charity funded the building of a community centre in the village and a memorial garden, which was opened by the <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen</a> in March 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller197449\xe2\x80\x9350_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller197449\xe2\x80\x9350-148">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Aberfan:_The_Fight_for_Justice&#39;&#39;,_18_October_2016Event_occurs_at_54:30\xe2\x80\x9354:55_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Aberfan:_The_Fight_for_Justice&#39;&#39;,_18_October_2016Event_occurs_at_54:30\xe2\x80\x9354:55-149">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> The garden is on the site of Pantglas Junior School and includes stone walls to show where the classrooms stood.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;Aberfan:_memorials_mark_50_years_since_tragedy_in_Wales&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Guardian&#39;&#39;_150-0" class="reference"><a
