href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;Aberfan:_memorials_mark_50_years_since_tragedy_in_Wales&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Guardian&#39;&#39;-150">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>McLean and Johnes consider that "the Commission protected neither donors nor beneficiaries. It was caught between upholding an outdated and inflexible law&#160;... and fulfilling the varied expectations of donors, beneficiaries and the fund\'s management committee".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000136_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000136-151">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> In a study of the fund, the UK government <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_Office" title="Cabinet Office">Cabinet Office</a> judged that "as far the fund is concerned and what it achieved, it is important to note that it did help in alleviating the suffering and was a focus for the grief of many".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;Aberfan_Disaster_\xe2\x80\x93_Financial_Support_for_Individuals&quot;,_Cabinet_Office_137-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;Aberfan_Disaster_\xe2\x80\x93_Financial_Support_for_Individuals&quot;,_Cabinet_Office-137">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> In 1988 the Aberfan Disaster Fund was separated into two entities: the Aberfan Memorial Charity and the Aberfan Disaster Fund and Centre, the second of which is administered by Merthyr Tydfil County Borough Council.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;The_Aberfan_Disaster_Fund_and_Centre&quot;,_The_Charity_Commission_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;The_Aberfan_Disaster_Fund_and_Centre&quot;,_The_Charity_Commission-152">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;The_Aberfan_Memorial_Charity&quot;,_The_Charity_Commission_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;The_Aberfan_Memorial_Charity&quot;,_The_Charity_Commission-153">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> The Aberfan Memorial Charity oversees the upkeep of the memorial garden and Bryntaf Cemetery, and provides financial assistance to "all those who have suffered as a result of the Aberfan Disaster by making grants of money or providing or paying for items, services or facilities calculated to reduce the need, hardship or distress of such persons".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;Trustees_Report_and_Unaudited_Financial_Statement&quot;,_The_Charity_Commission_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;Trustees_Report_and_Unaudited_Financial_Statement&quot;,_The_Charity_Commission-154">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Remaining_tips_and_the_fund">Remaining tips and the fund</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aberfan_disaster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Remaining tips and the fund">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aberfan_and_old_coal_tips_-_geograph.org.uk_-_673825.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Aberfan_and_old_coal_tips_-_geograph.org.uk_-_673825.jpg/220px-Aberfan_and_old_coal_tips_-_geograph.org.uk_-_673825.jpg" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Aberfan_and_old_coal_tips_-_geograph.org.uk_-_673825.jpg/330px-Aberfan_and_old_coal_tips_-_geograph.org.uk_-_673825.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Aberfan_and_old_coal_tips_-_geograph.org.uk_-_673825.jpg/440px-Aberfan_and_old_coal_tips_-_geograph.org.uk_-_673825.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="432" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aberfan_and_old_coal_tips_-_geograph.org.uk_-_673825.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The spoil heaps at Aberfan in 1968. <a href="/wiki/George_Thomas,_1st_Viscount_Tonypandy" title="George Thomas, 1st Viscount Tonypandy">George Thomas</a>, the Secretary of State for Wales, described them as "a psychological, emotional danger"; Tip 5 is furthest from the camera.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomas19671196\xe2\x80\x931197_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomas19671196\xe2\x80\x931197-155">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The tribunal report quoted one expert who said that Tip 5 "has been standing and is standing at a very low factor of safety";<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196747_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196747-156">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> the quote was read out by Thatcher in the October 1967 parliamentary debate on the inquiry report.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThatcher19671988\xe2\x80\x931990_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThatcher19671988\xe2\x80\x931990-157">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> S. O. Davies spoke in the debate on the same point:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>We must be under no illusion that the Aberfan tips have been made safe by today. They have not been made safe. There are two tips right at the top of the old tip, to be seen glaring at us every day, full of threat. They might come down and cover some part of the village again. The Aberfan people insist\xe2\x80\x94and I insist with them\xe2\x80\x94that what is left of those tips must be removed. I hope that the Minister and the Secretary of State for Wales will be with us on this matter.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies19671927\xe2\x80\x931929_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies19671927\xe2\x80\x931929-158">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>The residents of Aberfan petitioned <a href="/wiki/George_Thomas,_1st_Viscount_Tonypandy" title="George Thomas, 1st Viscount Tonypandy">George Thomas</a>, who had succeeded Hughes as Secretary of State for Wales in April 1968, for the tips to be removed; they entered the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Office" title="Welsh Office">Welsh Office</a> and left a small pile of coal slurry on the table in front of him to make their point; Thomas later stated the tips "constitute a psychological, emotional danger" to the people of Aberfan.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomas19671196\xe2\x80\x931197_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomas19671196\xe2\x80\x931197-155">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> The NCB had received a range of estimated costs for removing the tips, from \xc2\xa31.014&#160;million to \xc2\xa33.4&#160;million. Robens informed <a href="/wiki/HM_Treasury" title="HM Treasury">HM Treasury</a> that the cost would be \xc2\xa33&#160;million, and informed them that the NCB would not pay for the removal; between November 1967 and August he lobbied to avoid having the NCB pay. The <a href="/wiki/Chief_Secretary_to_the_Treasury" title="Chief Secretary to the Treasury">Chief Secretary to the Treasury</a> also refused to pay, and said that the costs were too high. Although the government had initially favoured landscaping\xe2\x80\x94an option cheaper than removal\xe2\x80\x94they were eventually persuaded that removal was preferable.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200035,_143_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200035,_143-159">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>To pay for the removal of the tips, \xc2\xa3150,000 was taken from the disaster fund\xe2\x80\x94lowered from the initial \xc2\xa3250,000 first requested\xe2\x80\x94the NCB paid \xc2\xa3350,000 and the government provided the balance, with the proviso it was only up to a million. The final cost of the removal was \xc2\xa3850,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200037\xe2\x80\x9338_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200037\xe2\x80\x9338-160">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> The trustees of the fund voted to accept the request for payment after realising that there was no alternative if they wanted the tips removed. S. O. Davies, the only member of the committee to vote against the payment, resigned in protest.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000144_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000144-161">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> There was a reminder of the danger for the residents of Aberfan when, in August 1968, heavy rain caused slurry to be washed down the village\'s streets.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000142_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000142-162">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> At the time, the Charity Commission made no objection to this action; the political scientists Jacint Jordana and <a href="/wiki/David_Levi-Faur" title="David Levi-Faur">David Levi-Faur</a> consider the payment "unquestionably unlawful" under charity law.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJordanaLevi-Faur200458_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJordanaLevi-Faur200458-163">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislation">Legislation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aberfan_disaster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Legislation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1969, as a result of concerns raised by the disaster, and in line with the findings of the tribunal report, the government framed new legislation to remedy the absence of laws and regulations governing mine and quarry spoil tips. The <a href="/wiki/Long_title" class="mw-redirect" title="Long title">long title</a> of the Mines and Quarries (Tips) Act 1969 was "An Act to make further provision in relation to tips associated with mines and quarries; to prevent disused tips constituting a danger to members of the public; and for purposes connected with those matters".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;Mines_And_Quarries_(Tips)_Act_1969&quot;1_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;Mines_And_Quarries_(Tips)_Act_1969&quot;1-164">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies1967132_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies1967132-165">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> The Act was an extension of the earlier Mines and Quarries Act 1954, which did not legislate over tips.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;Legislation_&amp;_Policy:_Mine_Waste&quot;,_British_Geological_Survey_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;Legislation_&amp;_Policy:_Mine_Waste&quot;,_British_Geological_Survey-166">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> According to McLean and Johnes, "the general commitment to public safety that the Tribunal had envisaged was not implemented" through the act, as the tribunal had advised wider legislation that should "consider the safety, health and welfare of all persons going about their lawful business in the vicinity of a mine, including the safety of their property".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000195\xe2\x80\x93196_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000195\xe2\x80\x93196-167">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 1970 <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Castle" title="Barbara Castle">Barbara Castle</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Employment_and_Productivity" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretary of State for Employment and Productivity">Secretary of State for Employment and Productivity</a>, appointed Robens to chair the Committee on Health and Safety at Work, to review legislation in the area and recommend the provisions that should be made for workers and the general public. In 1972 the committee published its findings in the Robens Report which led to the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Health_and_Safety_at_Work_etc._Act_1974" title="Health and Safety at Work etc. Act 1974">Health and Safety at Work etc. Act 1974</a> and the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Health_and_Safety_Commission" title="Health and Safety Commission">Health and Safety Commission</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Health_and_Safety_Executive" title="Health and Safety Executive">Health and Safety Executive</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;Committee_on_Safety_and_Health_at_Work_(Robens_Committee)&quot;,_The_National_Archives_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;Committee_on_Safety_and_Health_at_Work_(Robens_Committee)&quot;,_The_National_Archives-168">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;The_Robens_Report&quot;,_Health_and_Safety_Executive_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;The_Robens_Report&quot;,_Health_and_Safety_Executive-169">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aberfan_disaster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aberfan_Memorial_Garden_3031760_6dc3d0ac.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Aberfan_Memorial_Garden_3031760_6dc3d0ac.jpg/220px-Aberfan_Memorial_Garden_3031760_6dc3d0ac.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Aberfan_Memorial_Garden_3031760_6dc3d0ac.jpg/330px-Aberfan_Memorial_Garden_3031760_6dc3d0ac.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Aberfan_Memorial_Garden_3031760_6dc3d0ac.jpg/440px-Aberfan_Memorial_Garden_3031760_6dc3d0ac.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aberfan_Memorial_Garden_3031760_6dc3d0ac.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aberfan Memorial Garden in March 2012</div></div></div>\n<p>In addition to news and historical coverage, the Aberfan disaster and its aftermath have been described in books, including histories of what happened, personal memoirs from those involved and collections of poetry, in music, song and on film.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLean,_Iain._&quot;Books_About_Aberfan&quot;_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLean,_Iain._&quot;Books_About_Aberfan&quot;-170">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;n&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Merthyr Vale Colliery closed in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;High_Praise_for_Regeneration_of_Merthyr_Vale_Colliery_Site&quot;,_Merthyr_Tydfil_Council_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;High_Praise_for_Regeneration_of_Merthyr_Vale_Colliery_Site&quot;,_Merthyr_Tydfil_Council-185">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> In 1997 <a href="/wiki/Ron_Davies_(Welsh_politician)" title="Ron Davies (Welsh politician)">Ron Davies</a>, the Secretary of State for Wales in the incoming Labour government, repaid to the disaster fund the \xc2\xa3150,000 that it had been induced to contribute towards the cost of tip removal. No allowance was made for inflation or the interest that would have been earned over the intervening period, which would have been \xc2\xa31.5&#160;million in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Aberfan:_The_Fight_for_Justice&#39;&#39;,_18_October_2016Event_occurs_at_54:50\xe2\x80\x9356:35_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Aberfan:_The_Fight_for_Justice&#39;&#39;,_18_October_2016Event_occurs_at_54:50\xe2\x80\x9356:35-186">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000146\xe2\x80\x9347_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes2000146\xe2\x80\x9347-187">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> The payment was made in part after Iain McLean\'s examination of the papers released by the government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;Aberfan:_Prince_of_Wales_among_those_marking_disaster&#39;s_50th_anniversary&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Guardian&#39;&#39;_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;Aberfan:_Prince_of_Wales_among_those_marking_disaster&#39;s_50th_anniversary&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Guardian&#39;&#39;-188">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> In February 2007 the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Government" title="Welsh Government">Welsh Government</a> announced a donation of \xc2\xa31.5 million to the Aberfan Memorial Charity and \xc2\xa3500,000 to the Aberfan Education Charity, which represented an inflation-adjusted amount of the money taken.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Aberfan:_The_Fight_for_Justice&#39;&#39;,_18_October_2016Event_occurs_at_56:35\xe2\x80\x9357:50_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&#39;&#39;Aberfan:_The_Fight_for_Justice&#39;&#39;,_18_October_2016Event_occurs_at_56:35\xe2\x80\x9357:50-189">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> The money to the memorial charity was used in the upkeep of the memorials to the disaster.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen2011_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen2011-190">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 1997 the Queen and the Duke of Edinburgh planted a tree at the Aberfan Memorial Garden.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;1997:_The_Queen_revisits_Aberfan&quot;,_BBC_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;1997:_The_Queen_revisits_Aberfan&quot;,_BBC-191">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> In October 2016, the fiftieth anniversary of the disaster, memorial events took place at the garden and at the cemetery; the <a href="/wiki/Charles,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Charles, Prince of Wales">Prince of Wales</a> represented the Queen, and government ministers were present to pay tribute.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;Aberfan:_memorials_mark_50_years_since_tragedy_in_Wales&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Guardian&#39;&#39;_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;Aberfan:_memorials_mark_50_years_since_tragedy_in_Wales&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Guardian&#39;&#39;-150">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;Aberfan:_Prince_of_Wales_among_those_marking_disaster&#39;s_50th_anniversary&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Guardian&#39;&#39;_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;Aberfan:_Prince_of_Wales_among_those_marking_disaster&#39;s_50th_anniversary&quot;,_&#39;&#39;The_Guardian&#39;&#39;-188">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> At the time of the anniversary <a href="/wiki/Huw_Edwards_(journalist)" title="Huw Edwards (journalist)">Huw Edwards</a>, the <a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">BBC News</a> journalist and presenter, described the need to continue learning lessons from Aberfan; he wrote:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>What we can do, however\xe2\x80\x94in this week of the 50th anniversary\xe2\x80\x94is try to focus the attention of many in Britain and beyond on the lessons of Aberfan, lessons which are still of profound relevance today. They touch on issues of public accountability, responsibility, competence and transparency.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEdwards2016_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdwards2016-192">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes_and_references">Notes and references</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aberfan_disaster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Notes and references">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aberfan_disaster&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Only one tip at a time was ever used. They were begun in the following years:<div class="plainlist"><ul><li>Tip 1: during the First World War. 85 feet (26&#160;m) high and containing 235,000 cubic yards (180,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of spoil</li><li>Tip 2: 1918. 90 feet (27&#160;m) high, containing 574,000 cubic yards (439,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of spoil</li><li>Tip 3: 1925. 130 feet (40&#160;m) high, containing 210,000 cubic yards (160,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of spoil</li><li>Tip 4: 1933. 147 feet (45&#160;m) high, containing 572,000 cubic yards (437,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of spoil</li><li>Tip 5: 1945. 171 feet (52&#160;m) high, containing 706,000 cubic yards (540,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of spoil</li><li>Tip 6: 1956. 56 feet (17&#160;m) high, containing 67,000 cubic yards (51,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of spoil</li><li>Tip 7: Easter 1958. 111 feet (34&#160;m) high, containing 297,000 cubic yards (227,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup>) of spoil<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin19678\xe2\x80\x9310_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin19678\xe2\x80\x9310-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196713\xe2\x80\x9318_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196713\xe2\x80\x9318-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller197421\xe2\x80\x9322_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller197421\xe2\x80\x9322-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></div></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-30">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Small sinkings were not uncommon on the tips, normally measuring 3\xe2\x80\x934 feet (90\xe2\x80\x93120 cm).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin196713_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin196713-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-32">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The tipping crew saw the landslide start but were unable to raise the alarm because their telephone cable had been stolen. The official inquiry established that the slip happened so fast that a telephone warning would not have saved any lives.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196728_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196728-31">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-40"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-40">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Williams explained to the inquiry that "Being of the nature of a liquid the whole mass then moved very rapidly down the hillside, spreading out sideways into a layer of substantially uniform thickness. As this happened, water was escaping from the mass so that the particles of soil regained their contact and the soil mass returned to its solid nature."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196726\xe2\x80\x9327_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196726\xe2\x80\x9327-33">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-55"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-55">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It takes over an hour to shut down mains water supplies, and the valves for the feeder pipes, which needed to be operated manually, were spread out over several branches. Even once they were closed, there were still at least two miles of water-filled pipes that drained into the disaster area.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin196739\xe2\x80\x9340_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin196739\xe2\x80\x9340-54">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-79"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-79">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">There were two further deaths attributed to the disaster: a 19-year-old youth (the brother of a boy saved from the school) who collapsed and died from heart trouble while taking part in the rescue, and a 22-year-old soldier who had been assisting with the clear-up who died while hitch-hiking back to his regiment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAustin1967226_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAustin1967226-78">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-83"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-83">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Challenged by <a href="/wiki/John_Hobson_(politician)" title="John Hobson (politician)">John Hobson</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Loyal_opposition" title="Loyal opposition">opposition</a> MP, for trying to "stifle all comment" on the unlikely basis that an experienced judge could be swayed by it, the Attorney General was eventually persuaded by a <a href="/wiki/Backbencher" title="Backbencher">backbencher</a> of his own party to moderate his apparent initial position: speculation was unobjectionable, but issues must not be prejudged, and the "examination of potential witnesses on television and in the press" should be avoided.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJones19661315\xe2\x80\x931320_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJones19661315\xe2\x80\x931320-82">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-105"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-105">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Those named in the report are:\n<ul><li>Unit Mechanical Engineer: as a mechanical engineer, he was not trained in ensuring tip stability. Although he was present when the site for Tip 7 was chosen, the committee thought he bore no responsibility for the choice made.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196793\xe2\x80\x9394_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196793\xe2\x80\x9394-96">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Manager, Merthyr Vale Colliery: not a civil engineer by training, although the tribunal considered it was "inconceivable that&#160;...[he] should have failed to detect a most unusual state of affairs [at Tip 7] had he taken proper care".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196794\xe2\x80\x9395_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196794\xe2\x80\x9395-97">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Group Mechanical Engineer: a practical mechanical engineer, untrained in soil mechanics or tip stability. As someone who had selected four of the tip sites\xe2\x80\x94including for Tips 4 and 7\xe2\x80\x94the tribunal considered that he "must be blamed in some measure for starting tip 7". Although there had been slips previously, he had not considered or discussed the possible causes with anyone, which he should have done.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196796\xe2\x80\x9397_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196796\xe2\x80\x9397-98">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Group Manager: One of the three men who decided on the location of Tip 7. The tribunal stated that "ordinary intelligence should have alerted him to the fact that the new tip must be kept within a strictly limited area unless drainage and other problems were attended to", which they were not. He never visited the tips after making his decision, and the tribunal reported that "We cannot think that a Group Manager with a due sense of responsibility would have acted\xe2\x80\x94or, rather, wholly failed to act\xe2\x80\x94in all the circumstances as&#160;...[he] knew them to be".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196797\xe2\x80\x9398_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196797\xe2\x80\x9398-99">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Area Mechanical Engineer: deemed a diligent worker, he was untrained in tip stability and had received no guidance on the matter from his superiors. He was criticised for not taking seriously letters from Merthyr Tydfil Council about the possibility of slippage, and for not liaising with the Area Civil Engineer about the tips. The tribunal reported that "All things considered, and although he is doubtless a good, overworked and conscientious man,&#160;... [he] must shoulder a heavy portion of the blame for its occurrence."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196798\xe2\x80\x9399_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196798\xe2\x80\x9399-100">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Area Civil Engineer: he had visited the tip in April 1965 and, although he claimed not to have seen anything untoward, the tribunal considered that "it is impossible to understand how, with his trained eyes, he could have failed to detect those unusual signs visible in the photographs". Personal dislike of the Area Mechanical Engineer meant the two men did not liaise with one another, and the Area Civil Engineer should, like the Area Mechanical Engineer, take a heavy share of the blame.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies196799\xe2\x80\x93100_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies196799\xe2\x80\x93100-101">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Division Mechanical Engineer: in charge of the mechanical engineers who were supposed to oversee tip stability\xe2\x80\x94among other duties. He had never visited the tips at Aberfan, despite having visited the colliery several times, and had even discussed alterations to tipping procedure there. Although he was aware of the potential of tips to cause fatalities through slippage, he did not discuss the matter with the right people, and "did nothing towards the curing of the situation", according to the tribunal report.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies1967100\xe2\x80\x93102_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies1967100\xe2\x80\x93102-102">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Chief Engineer (SW Division): had responsibility for tip management and control. The tribunal censured him for failing to question why there was no tipping policy, because he did not introduce relevant procedures, and to review what poor system was already in place.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies1967103\xe2\x80\x93105_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies1967103\xe2\x80\x93105-103">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Production Director (SW Division): although he was aware of previous slips in Welsh coalfields and of the potential for danger, he had not visited Merthyr Vale since 1960, and stated that he had not heard of the slip that occurred there in 1963. The tribunal stated that the failure to introduce a rigorous tipping policy "undoubtedly contributed materially to the disaster".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies1967105\xe2\x80\x93107_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies1967105\xe2\x80\x93107-104">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n</span></li>\n<li id="cite_note-123"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-123">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Although it was possible in some circumstances for a corporate body to be prosecuted on some grounds,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200040\xe2\x80\x9341_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanJohnes200040\xe2\x80\x9341-121">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> not until the passage of the <a href="/wiki/Corporate_Manslaughter_and_Corporate_Homicide_Act_2007" title="Corporate Manslaughter and Corporate Homicide Act 2007">Corporate Manslaughter and Corporate Homicide Act 2007</a> was it possible for an organisation to be found guilty of <a href="/wiki/Corporate_manslaughter" title="Corporate manslaughter">corporate manslaughter</a> as a result of serious management failures resulting in a gross breach of a duty of care.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE&quot;About_Corporate_Manslaughter&quot;,_&#39;&#39;Health_and_Safety_Executive&#39;&#39;_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;About_Corporate_Manslaughter&quot;,_&#39;&#39;Health_and_Safety_Executive&#39;&#39;-122">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-133"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-133">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">\xc2\xa350 in 1967 equates to around \xc2\xa3820 in 2017; \xc2\xa3500 equates to around \xc2\xa38,200 over the same dates, according to calculations based on <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Price_Index_(United_Kingdom)" title="Consumer Price Index (United Kingdom)">Consumer Price Index</a> measure of inflation.<sup id="cite_ref-inflation-UK_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inflation-UK-132">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-138"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-138">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">\xc2\xa31.75&#160;million in 1966 equates to a little under \xc2\xa330&#160;million in 2017, according to calculations based on <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Price_Index_(United_Kingdom)" title="Consumer Price Index (United Kingdom)">Consumer Price Index</a> measure of inflation.<sup id="cite_ref-inflation-UK_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inflation-UK-132">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-146"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-146">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">\xc2\xa3100 in 1967 equates to \xc2\xa31,600 in 2017, according to calculations based on <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Price_Index_(United_Kingdom)" title="Consumer Price Index (United Kingdom)">Consumer Price Index</a> measure of inflation.<sup id="cite_ref-inflation-UK_132-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inflation-UK-132">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-147"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-147">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">\xc2\xa3100,000 in 1967 equates to a \xc2\xa31.63&#160;million in 2017; \xc2\xa35,000 equates to just under \xc2\xa382,000 over the same dates, according to calculations based on <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Price_Index_(United_Kingdom)" title="Consumer Price Index (United Kingdom)">Consumer Price Index</a> measure of inflation.<sup id="cite_ref-inflation-UK_132-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inflation-UK-132">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-184"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-184">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In print:\n<ul><li><i>Aberfan: Under the Arc Lights</i> (1966) a poem by <a href="/wiki/Keidrych_Rhys" title="Keidrych Rhys">Keidrych Rhys</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERhys196622_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERhys196622-171">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><i>Dagrau Tost: Cerddi Aber-fan</i> (<a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a>&#160;for <i>Bitter Tears: Aberfan Poems</i>; class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE&quot;Memories_stirred_by_Aberfan_poetry_collection&quot;,_Cardiff_University-172">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><i>The Riddle of the Pyramids</i>
